                        </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(4)</span></div>where Δ<i>t</i>, <i>m</i><sub>B</sub>, <i>M</i><sub>B</sub>, <i>V</i><sub>M</sub>, and <i>S</i> represent the pulse time (s), mass of active substance (g), molar quality (g mol<sup>−1</sup>), molar volume (cm<sup>3</sup> mol<sup>−1</sup>), and active surface area of the electrode (cm<sup>2</sup>), respectively. The Δ<i>E</i><sub>S</sub> and Δ<i>E</i><sub>τ</sub> can be calculated according to the GITT curves. The lower overpotentials of the Bi@NC for sodiation and desodiation suggest the fast-kinetic process. The sodium ions diffusion coefficients of Bi@NC and Bi at different potentials corresponding to the process of sodiation and desodiation are presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202304265-fig-0006">6f</a>. Although the diffusion coefficients of Bi@NC and Bi electrodes are both within the range between 10<sup>−7</sup> and 10<sup>−10</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, it is clear the Bi@NC electrode exhibits a higher diffusion coefficient than that of pure Bi. This result further evidences the fact that the N-doped carbon framework can expose more active sites on the electrode surface, thereby improving the kinetic performance of the overall electrode. Therefore, the resultant Bi@NC composite electrode is beneficial to improve the rate performance and long-term cycle performance of SIBs.</div>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202304265-sec-0050">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="smll202304265-sec-0050-title">2.3 Electrochemical Performance of Sodium Ions Full-Cell</h3>
            
            <p>The excellent performance of the Bi@NC electrode in the half-cell configuration reveals that the composite is a promising anode material for SIBs. Therefore, it is of great significance to comprehensively evaluate the application potential of the Bi@NC composite in the full-cell. As the schematic illustration shown in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#smll202304265-fig-0007">7a</a>, the synthesized NVP is designated as the cathode for its high voltage plateau and Bi@NC is appointed as the anode to assemble the NVP//Bi@NC full-cell. During a discharge process, sodium ions are escaped from the Bi@NC anode and migrated to the electrolyte. Meanwhile, <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/351bb7f0-2590-4b11-8d14-c77e474fe3d4/smll202304265-math-0005.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16136810:media:smll202304265:smll202304265-math-0005" display="inline" location="graphic/smll202304265-math-0005.png">
                  <semantics>
                     <msubsup>
                        <mi>PF</mi>
                        <mn>6</mn>
                        <mo>−</mo>
                     </msubsup>
                     <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${\mathrm{PF}}_6^ - $</annotation>
                  </semantics></math> is transferred from the cathode to anode. Contrary to the discharging process, sodium ions in the charge process is migrated and finally embedded in the Bi@NC anode while <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/f89f8b27-e6e2-4b68-8c27-0d38ac72097e/smll202304265-math-0006.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16136810:media:smll202304265:smll202304265-math-0006" display="inline" location="graphic/smll202304265-math-0006.png">
                  <semantics>
                     <msubsup>
                        <mi>PF</mi>
                        <mn>6</mn>
                        <mo>−</mo>
                     </msubsup>
                     <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${\mathrm{PF}}_6^ - $</annotation>
                  </semantics></math> flows toward the cathode. The resultant voltage distribution of NVP (2.6–3.8&nbsp;V) and Bi@NC (0.01–1.5&nbsp;V) are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202304265-fig-0007">7b</a>. Moreover, the detailed morphology and electrochemical performance of NVP are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a> (Supporting Information). It is evident that at a current density of 1C, the NVP electrode exhibits a specific capacity of 108.2&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and there is no obvious attenuation after 2000 constant current charge/discharge cycles. For the assembled full battery, the mass ratio of the active material between anode and cathode is regulated at ≈4:1 based upon the capacity matching principle. According to the voltage difference between the NVP cathode and the Bi@NC anode, the NVP//Bi@NC full-cell was explored within the potential window of 1.9–3.2&nbsp;V (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202304265-fig-0007">7c</a>). It is observed the resulting galvanostatic charge/discharge profiles of the full-cell present two voltage plateaus at 2.6 and 2.8&nbsp;V. The output stable voltage platform is conducive to the practical commercial application of sodium-ion batteries. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202304265-fig-0007">7d</a> shows the CV curves for the first three cycles of the full-cell at 0.2&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. The CV profile of full-cell presents two pairs of redox peaks at 2.5/2.7 and 2.7/2.9&nbsp;V, respectively, which are consistent with the charge/discharge process in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202304265-fig-0007">7c</a>. Meantime, the as-revealed charge/discharge profiles of different cycles are almost overlap, evidencing the constructed NVP//Bi@NC full-cell has excellent electrochemical reversibility and cycling stability.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="smll202304265-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/79270480-85a2-419e-835d-12c46fd9446f/smll202304265-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/79270480-85a2-419e-835d-12c46fd9446f/smll202304265-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/c0e115ea-ce25-40b6-b088-4473aec06ee3/smll202304265-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/79270480-85a2-419e-835d-12c46fd9446f/smll202304265-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202304265-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202304265" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performance of NVP//Bi@NC full-cell. a) Schematic illustration. b) GCD profiles of the NVP and Bi@NC at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. c) GCD profiles of the full-cell at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. d) CV profiles at 0.2&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. e) Rate capability at 0.1–10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. f) Long-term cycling stability at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> for 2000 cycles (inset: the coin full-cell is able to drive an electric fan).</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202304265-fig-0007">7e</a>, the rate performance of NVP//Bi@NC at various current densities reflects that the full-cell presents superior stabilities at different rates. When the current density increases from 0.1 to 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the NVP//Bi@NC full-cell exhibits high specific capacities from 258.4 to 252.2&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (calculated based on the mass of anode). It is worth noting that even at a high current density of 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the discharge specific capacity of the full-cell still retains well. Furthermore, the GCD curves of NVP//Bi@NC full-cell at different current densities and cycles are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a> (Supporting Information). The capacities hardly decreased with the increase of current density, reflecting a robust rate capability and superior structural stability of the Bi@NC electrode. In addition to the excellent rate performance, the NVP//Bi@NC full-cell also exhibits&nbsp;superior long-term cycle stability (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202304265-fig-0007">7f</a>). At a high current density of 5.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the full-cell can deliver a high reversible capacity of 251.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (with respective to the weight of Bi@NC composite). After 2000 long-term cycles, the full-cell can still maintain a high capacity of 204.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (capacity retention rate of 81.5%) and the coulombic efficiency is as high as 99.7%, proving the outstanding cycling stability. Thanks to the extraordinary energy and power characteristics of Bi@NC electrode, the coin-type full-cell itself can drive a small electric fan without assembling a large pouch battery (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a>, Supporting Information). These comprehensive outstanding properties of NVP//Bi@NC full-cell clearly indicate that the Bi@NC composite can be utilized as a feasible anode material for SIBs.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202304265-sec-0060">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="smll202304265-sec-0060-title">2.4 Theoretical Simulations</h3>
            
            <p>In addition to the experimental investigation, an in-depth theoretical analysis based on the first-principle simulations are carried out to gain insight into the effects of the N-doped carbon structures on the Na adsorption performance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202304265-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202304265-bib-0030_R_d126352089e1539" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - J. Mater. Chem. A Small Methods">30</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the DFT calculation, four types of projection structures are considered, including Bi embedded into carbon (Bi─C), Bi embedded into N-doped carbon (Bi─NC), Na adsorption on the Bi@C layer (Na─Bi@C), and Na adsorption on the Bi@NC layer (Na─Bi@NC), as shown in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#smll202304265-fig-0008">8</a>. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202304265-fig-0008">8a,b</a> presents the top view of Bi─C and Bi─NC structures, corresponding to the adsorption energy (Δ<i>E</i><sub>a</sub>) of −0.16 and −2.62&nbsp;eV. In general, higher adsorption energy values (|Δ<i>E</i><sub>a</sub>|) in the atomic structure usually correspond to stronger attractive propensities. The higher |Δ<i>E</i><sub>a</sub>| value of Bi─NC indicates that the binding force of N-doped carbon matrix to Bi is promoted, which is beneficial to improve the stability of carbon framework anchored Bi nanostructures. Compared with the Δ<i>E</i><sub>a</sub> of −1.51&nbsp;eV for the Bi@C structure (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202304265-fig-0008">8c</a>), the Bi@NC possesses the Δ<i>E</i><sub>a</sub> of −2.84&nbsp;eV (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202304265-fig-0008">8d</a>), indicating that the N-doped carbon framework has an obvious advantage in enhancing the adsorption energy for sodium ions. Simultaneously, the difference in electron density is helpful to comprehend the bonding properties of the adsorbed sodium. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202304265-fig-0008">8e–l</a> illustrates the top and side views of various types of structures, which further verify their robust combination.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202304265-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202304265-bib-0031_R_d126352089e1578" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Small Phys. Lett. A">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> On account of these comprehensive analyses, N-doped carbon materials with stronger adsorption energy always have higher charge density for sodium ions. By comparison, the Na─Bi@NC structure with strong adsorption energy indicates it is beneficial to the migration of sodium ions toward the active sites of Bi@NC electrode. The DFT results reveal that the N-doped carbon anchored Bi is more conducive to increasing the adsorption of sodium ions. This indicates that the synergistic effect of carbon framework and nitrogen doping can effectively enhance the sodium storage and kinetic performance. Therefore, the DFT calculation results support the experimental data in this study.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="smll202304265-fig-0008"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/c3660867-102e-4750-a4f1-3566c673eb64/smll202304265-fig-0008-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/c3660867-102e-4750-a4f1-3566c673eb64/smll202304265-fig-0008-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/8bbf73eb-4a65-47d3-a252-541ea66c0faf/smll202304265-fig-0008-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/c3660867-102e-4750-a4f1-3566c673eb64/smll202304265-fig-0008-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 8<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202304265-fig-0008&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202304265" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Sodium adsorption theoretical simulations. Models used to calculate the adsorption energy of Bi atoms on the top of a) C and b) NC layer. Models used to calculate the adsorption energy of Na atoms on the c) Bi@C and d) Bi@NC layer. e–l) The top and side view of charge density differences for the corresponding structure. C, N, Bi, and Na atoms are presented by brown, silver, purple, and yellow balls, respectively.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202304265-sec-0070">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202304265-sec-0070-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, novel Bi@NC composites with well-designed Bi nanoflowers uniformly encapsulated in the N-doped carbon framework are constructed as advanced anode materials for SIBs via an inexpensive, facile and scalable strategy. As for sodium-ion half-cell, the Bi@NC anode exhibits a high specific capacity (384.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) and excellent rate performance (341.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), and the capacity retention rate remains at 94.9% after 5000 cycles at 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Furthermore, the assembled NVP//Bi@NC full-cell can deliver a high capacity of 251.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, and its capacity attenuates only 0.009% in each cycle after 2000 times at 5.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. The DFT theoretical simulations further confirmed the positive effect of the N-doped carbon framework on modifying the electronic structure of Bi nanoflowers and enhancing the adsorption performance for Na ions. On the whole, this work presents an attractive pathway on the design of high-efficiency energy storage electrodes and the findings provide new prospects for the commercial realization of long-life, low-cost, and high-performance sodium ions batteries.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202304265-sec-0080">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202304265-sec-0080-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202304265-sec-0090">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202304265-sec-0100">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202304265-sec-0110">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202304265-sec-0110-title"> Synthesis of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub></h4>
                  
                  <p>In a typical process, 0.5&nbsp;g polyvinylpyrrolidone (PVP) and 0.3&nbsp;g thiourea (CH<sub>4</sub>N<sub>2</sub>S) were dispersed in 60&nbsp;mL ethylene glycol (EG) with magnetic stirring at 60&nbsp;°C to form a uniform solution. Then, 0.485&nbsp;g Bi(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>·5H<sub>2</sub>O was dissolved in 10&nbsp;mL EG and added dropwise to the above solution. The solution was placed in a thermostatic water bath at 65&nbsp;°C and stirred for 30&nbsp;min, then transferred to a polytetrafluoroethylene autoclave for solvothermal reaction at 140&nbsp;°C and kept for 8&nbsp;h. After the reactor was cooled to the room temperature, the black product was washed with deionized water and ethanol, and finally collected by suction filtration. Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> nanoflowers were obtained after drying in a vacuum oven at 60&nbsp;°C for 12&nbsp;h.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202304265-sec-0120">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202304265-sec-0120-title"> Synthesis of Bi@NC</h4>
                  
                  <p>Coal tar pitch (CTP) (0.2&nbsp;g) was dissolved in 10&nbsp;ml <i>N, N</i>-Dimethylformamide (DMF) under magnetic stirring for 2&nbsp;h. Then, 0.2&nbsp;g Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and 4.0&nbsp;g ultrafine NaCl (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a>, Supporting Information) were added to the obtained solution and ultrasonic treated for 1&nbsp;h to get uniform dispersion. The excess DMF was then removed by evaporation at 80&nbsp;°C in the fume hood. The obtained dark-brown product was transferred into a tubular furnace and heated to 550&nbsp;°C in a 40 SCCM flowing gas (NH<sub>3</sub>/Ar ratio of 1:9) atmosphere held for 2&nbsp;h and then switch the atmosphere to H<sub>2</sub>/Ar (1:9) under the same conditions. After cooling naturally, the obtained samples were rinsed with deionized water. During this process, the NaCl salt template could be leached away for another recycle use. Finally, the composite electrode material of bismuth nanoflowers encapsulated in N-doped carbon frameworks was achieved (marked as Bi@NC). Meanwhile, a sample of pure bismuth nanoparticles was also synthesized for comparison. The detailed process is as follows: Bi (NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>·5H<sub>2</sub>O (0.970&nbsp;g) and NaBH<sub>4</sub> (0.38&nbsp;g) were respectively dissolved in 30&nbsp;mL of deionized water and stirred for 2&nbsp;h. The two solutions were then mixed for complete reaction. The black precipitate was washed several times with deionized water and vacuum dried at 60&nbsp;°C for 10&nbsp;h to obtain pure bismuth (marked as Bi).</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202304265-sec-0130">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202304265-sec-0130-title"> Synthesis of NVP</h4>
                  
                  <p>The Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVP) was synthesized with reference to the work by Yang et&nbsp;al.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202304265-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202304265-bib-0032_R_d126352089e1714" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - J. Power Sources">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The NaH<sub>2</sub>PO<sub>4</sub>: NH<sub>4</sub>VO<sub>3</sub>: C<sub>6</sub>H<sub>12</sub>O<sub>6</sub> were dispersed to ethyl alcohol at the weight ratio of 4.21: 2.74: 1.23. The composite slurry was then transferred to an agate tank and ground using a planetary ball mill at 400&nbsp;rpm for 10&nbsp;h. After the above procedure, slurry was transferred to the blast drying oven to remove the excess alcohol and then calcined at 800&nbsp;°C in tubular furnace for 4&nbsp;h at the atmosphere of flowing H<sub>2</sub>/Ar (H<sub>2</sub>/Ar ratio of 1:9) to form the NVP.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202304265-sec-0140">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202304265-sec-0140-title"> Microstructure Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>The crystal structure of as-obtained composites was analyzed using an X-ray diffraction (XRD; DX-2700 X-ray diffractometer) instrument with Cu Kα radiation (<i>λ</i> = 1.5406&nbsp;Å) operated at 40&nbsp;kV and 30&nbsp;mA. The morphological feature was investigated by scanning electron microscopy (SEM; JSM-7900F) and the detailed microstructure and crystallinity were determined by transmission electron microscopy (TEM; JEM-F200). The thermos-gravimetric analysis (TGA) was carried out on synchronous thermal analyzer (NETZSCH, STA449F3, Germany) with a rate of 10&nbsp;°C&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup> in an air atmosphere. Raman spectra were characterized with a DXR Raman Microscope (Thermal Scientific, the laser excitation was 532&nbsp;nm). X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS; Thermo Scientific K-Alpha) was performed for the surface chemical state of the composites. The Brunauer–Emmett–Teller (BET; BSD-PS2) test was carried out using nitrogen as the adsorbent gas to detect specific surface area and pore diameter.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202304265-sec-0150">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202304265-sec-0150-title"> Electrochemical Measurements</h4>
                  
                  <p>The Bi@NC anode and NVP cathode were prepared by mixing 80&nbsp;wt.% Bi@NC or NVP active material, 10&nbsp;wt.% carbon black, and 10&nbsp;wt.% polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF) binder. <i>N</i>-Methyl-2-pyrrolidone (NMP) was employed as solvent to prepare a uniform slurry. The as-prepared slurry was coated on Cu foil for Bi@NC anode and Al foil for NVP cathode. After vacuum drying at 80&nbsp;°C for 12&nbsp;h, the electrodes were punched into circular pieces. Sodium metal was used as the counter electrode and reference electrode for half-cell. Glass fiber membrane (Whatman GF/D) was worked as a separator and 1.0&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaPF<sub>6</sub> dissolved in 1, 2-dimethoxyethane (DME) was served as electrolyte. The CR2032 coin cells were assembled in an Ar filled glove box (Mikrouna, Super 1220) to evaluate the electrochemical performances of both half and full cells. The active mass loading of Bi@NC anode was controlled at ≈1&nbsp;mg cm<sup>−2</sup>. For the capacity matching of full cells, the mass ratio of NVP cathode to Bi@NC anode was adjusted to ≈4:1. Galvanostatic charge/discharge tests were performed on a battery test system (CT2001A, LAND) within a voltage range of 0.01–1.5&nbsp;V for the Bi@NC anode and 2.6–3.6&nbsp;V for the NVP cathode (vs. Na/Na<sup>+</sup>). At the current density of 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup>, galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) was executed with a current pulse duration of 10&nbsp;min and an interval period of 1&nbsp;h. Cyclic voltammetry (CV) measurements were performed on an electrochemical workstation (CS-2350H, CORRTEST) with a scanning rate from 0.1 to 1.0&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) was tested from 10<sup>5</sup> to 10<sup>−2</sup>&nbsp;Hz with an amplitude of 5.0&nbsp;mV.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202304265-sec-0160">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202304265-sec-0160-title"> Theoretical Simulations</h4>
                  
                  <p>The Vienna Ab Initial Simulation Package (VASP) code was used in this work for density functional theory (DFT) calculations.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202304265-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202304265-bib-0033_R_d126352089e1790" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Nano-Micro Lett.">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The electron projector-augmented wave methods were used with the PBE generalized gradient approximation (GGA) exchange correlation. In all calculations, the plane-wave kinetic cut-off energy was set to 370&nbsp;eV. The atoms and cells in all structures were relaxed until the convergence threshold reached to 10<sup>−4</sup>&nbsp;eV in energy and −0.02&nbsp;eV&nbsp;Å<sup>−1</sup> in force.</p>
                  
                  <div class="paragraph-element">The Brillouin zone was selected with a 3 × 3 × 1 <i>k</i>-point mesh. A supercell consisted of 6 × 6 × 1 graphite-like carbon was built and the vacuum space was set as 15&nbsp;Å vacuum in order to prevent the layer's interaction with each other. The absorbed energy was defined as:

                     <div class="inline-equation" id="smll202304265-disp-0005"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                           <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/93f2b179-3fb5-441b-8548-de74bf25d5b9/smll202304265-math-0007.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16136810:media:smll202304265:smll202304265-math-0007" display="block" location="graphic/smll202304265-math-0007.png">
                              <semantics>
                                 <mrow>
                                    <msub>
                                       <mi mathvariant="normal">E</mi>
                                       <mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
                                    </msub>
                                    <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                                    <msub>
                                       <mi mathvariant="normal">E</mi>
                                       <mrow>
                                          <mi>Na</mi>
                                          <mo>/</mo>
                                          <mi>surf</mi>
                                       </mrow>
                                    </msub>
                                    <mo linebreak="goodbreak">−</mo>
                                    <msub>
                                       <mi mathvariant="normal">E</mi>
                                       <mi>surf</mi>
                                    </msub>
                                    <mo linebreak="goodbreak">−</mo>
                                    <msub>
                                       <mi mathvariant="normal">E</mi>
                                       <mi>Na</mi>
                                    </msub>
                                 </mrow>
                                 <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{{\mathrm{E}}_{\mathrm{a}}} = {{\mathrm{E}}_{{\mathrm{Na/surf}}}}{\mathrm{ - }}{{\mathrm{E}}_{{\mathrm{surf}}}}{\mathrm{ - }}{{\mathrm{E}}_{{\mathrm{Na}}}}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                              </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(5)</span></div>Wherein <i>E</i><sub>Na</sub> is the energy of a Na atom in the bulk position, <i>E</i><sub>Na/surf</sub> is the total energy of the electrode with Na atom adsorbed, and <i>E</i><sub>surf</sub> is the energy without Na atom adsorbed, respectively. The VESTA was used as a 3D visualisation program software to illustrate the chemical structure of the models.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202304265-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202304265-bib-0034_R_d126352089e1849" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - J. Appl. Crystallogr.">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></div>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
